          This article contains
          <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">

          </a>
          phonetic symbols.
         </b>

         <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet#Fonts" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
          rendering support
         </a>
         , you may see
         <a href="/wiki/Specials_(Unicode_block)#Replacement_character" title="Specials (Unicode block)">
          question marks, boxes, or other symbols
         </a>
         instead of
         <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">
          Unicode
         </a>
         characters. For an introductory guide on IPA symbols, see
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">
          Help:IPA
         </a>
         .

      <p>
       This article is about the
       <a href="/wiki/Phonology" title="Phonology">
        phonology
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Phonetics" title="Phonetics">
        phonetics
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish language
       </a>
       . Unless otherwise noted, statements refer to
       <a href="/wiki/Castilian_Spanish" title="Castilian Spanish">
        Castilian Spanish
       </a>
       , the standard dialect used in
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       on radio and television.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For historical development of the sound system see
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Spanish" title="History of Spanish">
        History of Spanish
       </a>
       . For details of geographical variation see
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_dialects_and_varieties" title="Spanish dialects and varieties">
        Spanish dialects and varieties
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Spanish has many
       <a href="/wiki/Allophone" title="Allophone">
        allophones
       </a>
       , so it is important here to distinguish
       <a href="/wiki/Phoneme" title="Phoneme">
        phonemes
       </a>
       (written between slashes / /) and corresponding allophones (written between brackets [ ]).
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td rowspan="2" style="width: 25px;">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">

           ɡ

        </td>
       </tr>

        </td>
        <td style="border-left: 0;">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">

         </span>

        <td colspan="2">

        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The phonemes
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /b/
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /d/
       </span>
       , and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ɡ/
       </span>
       are realized as
       <a href="/wiki/Approximant_consonant" title="Approximant consonant">
        approximants
       </a>
       (namely
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bilabial_approximant" title="Bilabial approximant">
          β̞
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dental_approximant" title="Dental approximant">
          ð̞
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Voiced_velar_approximant" title="Voiced velar approximant">
          ɣ˕
         </a>
        </span>
        ]
       </span>
       , hereafter represented without the
       <a href="/wiki/Relative_articulation#Raised_and_lowered" title="Relative articulation">
        downtack
       </a>
       ) or
       <a href="/wiki/Fricative_consonant" title="Fricative consonant">
        fricatives
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in all places except after a pause, after a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nasal_stop" title="Nasal stop">
        nasal consonant
       </a>
       , or—in the case of
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /d/
       </span>
       —after a
       <a href="/wiki/Lateral_consonant" title="Lateral consonant">
        lateral consonant
       </a>
       ; in such contexts they are realized as voiced
       <a href="/wiki/Stop_consonant" title="Stop consonant">
        stops
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carrera257_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-carrera257-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The phoneme
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʝ/
       </span>
       is realized as an approximant in all contexts except after a pause, a nasal, or a lateral. In these environments, it may be realized as an
       <a href="/wiki/Affricate_consonant" title="Affricate consonant">
        affricate
       </a>
       (
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Voiced_palatal_affricate" title="Voiced palatal affricate">
         ɟʝ
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carrera258_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-carrera258-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trager_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Trager-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The approximant allophone differs from non-syllabic
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /i/
       </span>
       in a number of ways; it has a lower
       <a href="/wiki/Formant" title="Formant">
        F2
       </a>
       amplitude, is longer, can only appear in the syllable onset (including word-initially, where non-syllabic
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /i/
       </span>
       normally never appears), is a
       <a href="/wiki/Voiced_palatal_fricative" title="Voiced palatal fricative">
        palatal fricative
       </a>
       in emphatic pronunciations, and is unspecified for rounding (e.g.
       <i>
        v
        <b>
         iu
        </b>
        da
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈbjuða]
       </span>
       'widow' vs
       <i>
        a
        <b>
         yu
        </b>
        da
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [aˈʝʷuða]
       </span>
       'help').
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The two also overlap in distribution after
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /l/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /n/
       </span>
       :
       <i>
        en
        <b>
         ye
        </b>
        sar
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ẽɲɟʝeˈsaɾ]
       </span>
       ('to plaster')
       <i>
        an
        <b>
         ie
        </b>
        go
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [aˈnjeɣo]
       </span>
       ('flood').
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trager_9-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Trager-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Although there is dialectal and ideolectal variation, speakers may also exhibit other near-minimal pairs like
       <i>
        ab
        <b>
         ye
        </b>
        cto
       </i>
       ('abject') vs
       <i>
        ab
        <b>
         ie
        </b>
        rto
       </i>
       ('opened').
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are some
       <a href="#Alternations">
        alternations
       </a>
       between the two, prompting scholars like
       <a href="#CITEREFAlarcos_Llorach1950">
        Alarcos Llorach (1950)
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       to postulate an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archiphoneme" title="Archiphoneme">
        archiphoneme
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <span style="font-family: 'Georgia Pro', Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;">
         I
        </span>
        /
       </span>
       , so that
       <i>
        ley
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [lei̯]
       </span>
       would be transcribed phonemically as
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ˈle
        <span style="font-family: 'Georgia Pro', Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;">
         I
        </span>
        /
       </span>
       and
       <i>
        leyes
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈleʝes]
       </span>
       as
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ˈle
        <span style="font-family: 'Georgia Pro', Georgia, 'DejaVu Serif', Times, 'Times New Roman', serif;">
         I
        </span>
        es/
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In a number of varieties, including some American ones, a process parallel to the one distinguishing non-syllabic
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /i/
       </span>
       from consonantal
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʝ/
       </span>
       occurs for non-syllabic
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /u/
       </span>
       and a rare consonantal
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /w̝/
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trager_9-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Trager-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Near-minimal pairs include
       <i>
        des
        <b>
         hue
        </b>
        sar
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [dezw̝eˈsaɾ]
       </span>
       ('to bone') vs.
       <i>
        des
        <b>
         ue
        </b>
        llo
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [deˈsweʎo]
       </span>
       ('skinning'),
       <i>
        son
        <b>
         hue
        </b>
        vos
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈsõŋ ˈw̝eβos]
       </span>
       ('they are eggs') vs
       <i>
        son n
        <b>
         ue
        </b>
        vos
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈsõⁿ ˈnweβos]
       </span>
       ('they are new'),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <i>
        <b>
         hua
        </b>
        ca
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈ(ɡ)w̝aka]
       </span>
       ('Indian grave') vs
       <i>
        <b>
         u o
        </b>
        ca
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈwoka]
       </span>
       ('or goose').
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The phoneme
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʎ/
       </span>
       (as distinct from
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʝ/
       </span>
       ) is found in some areas in
       <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_Spanish" title="Peninsular Spanish">
        Spain
       </a>
       (mostly northern and rural) and some areas of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_American_Spanish" title="Latin American Spanish">
        South America
       </a>
       (mostly highlands).
      </p>
      <p>
       Most speakers in Spain (except for Western Andalusia and all Canary Islands), including the variety prevalent on radio and television, have both
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /θ/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       (
       <i>
        distinción
       </i>
       ). However, speakers in Latin America and those parts of southern Spain have only
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       (
       <i>
        seseo
       </i>
       ). Some speakers in southernmost Spain (especially coastal Andalusia) have only
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_corono-dentoalveolar_sibilant" title="Voiceless corono-dentoalveolar sibilant">
         s̄
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       (a consonant similar to
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /θ/
       </span>
       ) and not
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       (
       <i>
        ceceo
       </i>
       ). This "ceceo" is not entirely unknown in the Americas, especially in coastal Peru. The phoneme
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       has three different pronunciations ("laminal s", "apical s" or "apical dental s")
       <a href="#Realization_of_/s/">
        depending on dialect
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The phonemes
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /t/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /d/
       </span>
       are
       <a href="/wiki/Laminal_consonant" title="Laminal consonant">
        laminal
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Denti-alveolar_consonant" title="Denti-alveolar consonant">
        denti-alveolars
       </a>
       (
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_dental_and_alveolar_stops#Dental_or_denti-alveolar" title="Voiceless dental and alveolar stops">
          t̪
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Voiced_dental_and_alveolar_stops#Dental_or_denti-alveolar" title="Voiced dental and alveolar stops">
          d̪
         </a>
        </span>
        ]
       </span>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carrera257_7-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-carrera257-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The phoneme
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       becomes
       <a href="/wiki/Dental_consonant" title="Dental consonant">
        dental
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [s̪]
       </span>
       before denti-alveolar consonants,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carrera258_8-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-carrera258-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       while
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /θ/
       </span>
       remains
       <a href="/wiki/Interdental_consonant" title="Interdental consonant">
        interdental
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [θ̟]
       </span>
       in all contexts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carrera258_8-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-carrera258-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Before front vowels
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /i, e/
       </span>
       , the velar consonants
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /k, ɡ, x/
       </span>
       (including the lenited allophone of
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ɡ/
       </span>
       ) are realized as post-palatal
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_palatal_stop#Post-palatal" title="Voiceless palatal stop">
          k̟
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Voiced_palatal_stop#Post-palatal" title="Voiced palatal stop">
          ɡ˖
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_palatal_fricative#Post-palatal" title="Voiceless palatal fricative">
          x̟
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Palatal_approximant#Post-palatal" title="Palatal approximant">
          ɣ˕˖
         </a>
        </span>
        ]
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to some authors,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /x/
       </span>
       is
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_fricative#Voiceless_post-velar_fricative" title="Voiceless velar fricative">
        post-velar
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_uvular_fricative" title="Voiceless uvular fricative">
        uvular
       </a>
       in the Spanish of northern and central Spain.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Others
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       describe
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /x/
       </span>
       as velar in European Spanish, with a
       <a href="/wiki/Uvular_consonant" title="Uvular consonant">
        uvular
       </a>
       allophone (
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_uvular_fricative" title="Voiceless uvular fricative">
         χ
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       ) appearing before
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /u/
       </span>
       (including when
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /u/
       </span>
       is in the syllable onset as
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [w]
       </span>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carrera258_8-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-carrera258-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A common pronunciation of
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /f/
       </span>
       in nonstandard speech is the
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_bilabial_fricative" title="Voiceless bilabial fricative">
        voiceless bilabial fricative
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_bilabial_fricative" title="Voiceless bilabial fricative">
         ɸ
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       , so that
       <i>
        <b>
         f
        </b>
        uera
       </i>
       is pronounced
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈɸweɾa]
       </span>
       rather than
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈfweɾa]
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cotton15_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cotton15-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In some Extremaduran, western Andalusian, and American varieties, this softened realization of
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /f/
       </span>
       , when it occurs before
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /w/
       </span>
       , is subject to merger with
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /x/
       </span>
       ; in some areas the homophony of
       <i>
        fuego
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        juego
       </i>
       is resolved by replacing
       <i>
        fuego
       </i>
       with
       <i>
        lumbre
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        candela
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʃ/
       </span>
       is a marginal phoneme that occurs only in loanwords; many speakers have difficulty with this sound, tending to replace it with
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /tʃ/
       </span>
       or
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       . In a number of dialects (most notably, Northern Mexican Spanish, informal Chilean Spanish, and some Caribbean and Andalusian accents)
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_postalveolar_fricative" title="Voiceless postalveolar fricative">
         ʃ
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       occurs, as a
       <a href="/wiki/Lenition" title="Lenition">
        deaffricated
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /tʃ/
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cotton15_25-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-cotton15-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Consonant_neutralizations">
        Consonant neutralizations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Consonant neutralizations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Some of the
       <a href="/wiki/Phonemic_contrast" title="Phonemic contrast">
        phonemic contrasts
       </a>
       between consonants in Spanish are lost in certain phonological environments, and especially in syllable-final position. In these cases the phonemic contrast is said to be
       <a href="/wiki/Phoneme#Neutralization_and_archiphonemes" title="Phoneme">
        neutralized
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sonorants">
        Sonorants
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Sonorants">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Nasals and laterals
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <p>
       The three
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nasal_stop" title="Nasal stop">
        nasal phonemes
       </a>
       —
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /m/
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /n/
       </span>
       , and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ɲ/
       </span>
       —maintain their contrast when in syllable-initial position (e.g.
       <i>
        ca
        <b>
         m
        </b>
        a
       </i>
       'bed',
       <i>
        ca
        <b>
         n
        </b>
        a
       </i>
       'grey hair',
       <i>
        ca
        <b>
         ñ
        </b>
        a
       </i>
       'sugar cane'). In syllable-final position, this three-way contrast is lost as nasals assimilate to the
       <a href="/wiki/Place_of_articulation" title="Place of articulation">
        place of articulation
       </a>
       of the following consonant
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carrera258_8-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-carrera258-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       —even across a word boundary;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       or, if a nasal is followed by a pause rather than a consonant, it is realized for most speakers as alveolar
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [n]
       </span>
       (though in Caribbean varieties this may instead be
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Velar_nasal" title="Velar nasal">
         ŋ
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       or an omitted nasal with nasalization of the preceding vowel).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Thus
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /n/
       </span>
       is realized as
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [m]
       </span>
       before labial consonants, and as
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Velar_nasal" title="Velar nasal">
         ŋ
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       before velar ones.
      </p>
      <p>
       Similarly,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /l/
       </span>
       assimilates to the place of articulation of a following
       <a href="/wiki/Coronal_consonant" title="Coronal consonant">
        coronal consonant
       </a>
       , i.e. a consonant that is interdental, dental, alveolar, or palatal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dalbor_1980_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Dalbor_1980-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Assimilatory nasal and lateral allophones are shown in the following table:
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">

         <a href="/wiki/Lateral_consonant" title="Lateral consonant">
          lateral
         </a>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>

        </td>

         <b>

         </b>

         </span>

        </td>

       </tr>
      </table>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Rhotics
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_trill" title="Alveolar trill">
        alveolar trill
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_trill" title="Alveolar trill">
         r
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_tap" title="Alveolar tap">
        alveolar tap
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_flap" title="Alveolar flap">
         ɾ
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       are in phonemic contrast word-internally between vowels (as in
       <i>
        ca
        <b>
         rr
        </b>
        o
       </i>
       'car' vs
       <i>
        ca
        <b>
         r
        </b>
        o
       </i>
       'expensive'), but are otherwise in
       <a href="/wiki/Complementary_distribution" title="Complementary distribution">
        complementary distribution
       </a>
       . Only the trill can occur after
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /l/
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /n/
       </span>
       , or
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       (e.g.
       <i>
        al
        <b>
         r
        </b>
        ededor
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        en
        <b>
         r
        </b>
        iquecer
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        Is
        <b>
         r
        </b>
        ael
       </i>
       ), and word-initially (e.g.
       <i>
        <b>
         r
        </b>
        ey
       </i>
       'king'). After a stop or fricative consonant (but not
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       ), only the tap can occur (e.g.
       <i>
        t
        <b>
         r
        </b>
        es
       </i>
       'three',
       <i>
        f
        <b>
         r
        </b>
        ío
       </i>
       'cold').
      </p>
      <p>
       In syllable-final position, inside a word, the tap is more frequent, but the trill can also occur (especially in emphatic
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       or oratorical
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       style) with no semantic difference—thus
       <i>
        arma
       </i>
       ('weapon') may be either
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈaɾma]
       </span>
       (tap) or
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈarma]
       </span>
       (trill).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harris_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Harris-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <i>
        word
       </i>
       -final position the rhotic is usually:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        either a trill or a tap when followed by a consonant or a pause, as in
        <i>
         amo
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [r ~ ɾ]
        </span>
        <i>
         paterno
        </i>
        'paternal love'),
       </li>
       <li>
        a tap when followed by a vowel-initial word, as in
        <i>
         amo
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ɾ]
        </span>
        <i>
         eterno
        </i>
        'eternal love').
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       The tap/trill alternation has prompted a number of authors to postulate a single
       <a href="/wiki/Underlying_representation" title="Underlying representation">
        underlying
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Rhotic_consonant" title="Rhotic consonant">
        rhotic
       </a>
       ; the intervocalic contrast then results from
       <a href="/wiki/Gemination" title="Gemination">
        gemination
       </a>
       (e.g.
       <i>
        tierra
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ˈtieɾɾa/
       </span>
       &gt;
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈtjera]
       </span>
       'earth').
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Obstruents">
        Obstruents
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Obstruents">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The phonemes
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /θ/
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carrera258_8-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-carrera258-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /f/
       </span>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       become voiced before voiced consonants as in
       <i>
        jazmín
       </i>
       ('Jasmine')
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [xaðˈmĩn]
       </span>
       ,
       <i>
        rasgo
       </i>
       ('feature')
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈrazɣo]
       </span>
       , and
       <i>
        Afganistán
       </i>
       ('
       <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">
        Afghanistan
       </a>
       ')
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [avɣanisˈtãn]
       </span>
       . There is a certain amount of free variation in this so that
       <i>
        jazmín
       </i>
       can be pronounced
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [xaθˈmĩn]
       </span>
       or
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [xaðˈmĩn]
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Both in casual and in formal speech, there is no phonemic contrast between
       <a href="/wiki/Voice_(phonetics)" title="Voice (phonetics)">
        voiced and voiceless
       </a>
       consonants placed in syllable-final position. The merged phoneme is typically pronounced as a relaxed, voiced
       <a href="/wiki/Fricative_consonant" title="Fricative consonant">
        fricative
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Approximant_consonant" title="Approximant consonant">
        approximant
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       although a variety of other realizations are also possible. So the clusters -
       <i>
        bt
       </i>
       - and -
       <i>
        pt
       </i>
       - in the words
       <i>
        obtener
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        optimista
       </i>
       are pronounced exactly the same way:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <i>
         o
         <b>
          b
         </b>
         tener
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /obteˈner/ &gt; [oβteˈner]
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         o
         <b>
          p
         </b>
         timista
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /obtiˈmista/ &gt; [oβtiˈmista]
        </span>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Similarly, the spellings
       <i>
        -dm-
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        -tm-
       </i>
       are merged in pronunciation, as well as -
       <i>
        gd
       </i>
       - and -
       <i>
        cd
       </i>
       -:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <i>
         a
         <b>
          d
         </b>
         minículo
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /admiˈnikulo/ &gt; [aðmiˈnikulo]
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         a
         <b>
          t
         </b>
         mosférico
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /admosˈfeɾiko/ &gt; [aðmosˈfeɾiko]
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         amí
         <b>
          g
         </b>
         dala
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /aˈmiɡdala/ &gt; [aˈmiɣðala]
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         ané
         <b>
          c
         </b>
         dota
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /aˈneɡdota/ &gt; [aˈneɣðota]
        </span>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vowels">
        Vowels
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Vowels">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spanish_vowel_chart.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="746" data-file-width="982" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Spanish_vowel_chart.svg/250px-Spanish_vowel_chart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Spanish_vowel_chart.svg/375px-Spanish_vowel_chart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Spanish_vowel_chart.svg/500px-Spanish_vowel_chart.svg.png 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spanish_vowel_chart.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Spanish vowel chart, from
         <a href="#CITEREFLadefogedJohnson2010">
          Ladefoged &amp; Johnson (2010
         </a>
         :227)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th>
        </th>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Front_vowel" title="Front vowel">
          Front
         </a>
        </th>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Central_vowel" title="Central vowel">
          Central
         </a>
        </th>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Back_vowel" title="Back vowel">
          Back
         </a>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr style="text-align: center;">
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Close_vowel" title="Close vowel">
          Close
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Close_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close front unrounded vowel">
           i
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Close_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close back rounded vowel">
           u
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr style="text-align: center;">
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Mid_vowel" title="Mid vowel">
          Mid
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Mid front unrounded vowel">
           e
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Mid back rounded vowel">
           o
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr style="text-align: center;">
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Open_vowel" title="Open vowel">
          Open
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          <a href="/wiki/Open_central_unrounded_vowel" title="Open central unrounded vowel">
           a
          </a>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Spanish has five vowels
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /i/
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /u/
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /e/
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /o/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /a/
       </span>
       . Each occurs in both stressed and unstressed syllables:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carrera256_49-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-carrera256-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="3">
         stressed
        </th>
        <th colspan="3">
         unstressed
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2">
         word
        </th>
        <th>
         gloss
        </th>
        <th colspan="2">
         word
        </th>
        <th>
         gloss
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         p
         <b>
          i
         </b>
         so
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ˈpiso/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'I step'
        </td>
        <td>
         p
         <b>
          i
         </b>
         só
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /piˈso/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         's/he stepped'
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         p
         <b>
          u
         </b>
         jo
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ˈpuxo/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'I bid' (present tense)
        </td>
        <td>
         p
         <b>
          u
         </b>
         jó
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /puˈxo/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         's/he bid'
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         p
         <b>
          e
         </b>
         so
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ˈpeso/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'I weigh'
        </td>
        <td>
         p
         <b>
          e
         </b>
         só
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /peˈso/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         's/he weighed'
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         p
         <b>
          o
         </b>
         so
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ˈposo/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'I pose'
        </td>
        <td>
         p
         <b>
          o
         </b>
         só
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /poˈso/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         's/he posed'
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         p
         <b>
          a
         </b>
         so
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ˈpaso/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'I pass'
        </td>
        <td>
         p
         <b>
          a
         </b>
         só
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /paˈso/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         's/he passed'
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Nevertheless, there are some distributional gaps or rarities. For instance, an unstressed
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_vowel" title="High vowel">
        high vowel
       </a>
       in the final syllable of a word is rare.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Because of substratal Quechua, at least some speakers from southern Colombia down through Peru can be analyzed to have only three vowel phonemes
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /i, u, a/
       </span>
       , as the close
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [i, u]
       </span>
       are continually confused with the mid
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [e, o]
       </span>
       , resulting in pronunciations such as
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [dolˈsoɾa]
       </span>
       for
       <i>
        dulzura
       </i>
       ('sweetness'). When Quechua-dominant bilinguals have
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /e, o/
       </span>
       in their phonemic inventory, they realize them as
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Near-close_near-front_unrounded_vowel" title="Near-close near-front unrounded vowel">
          ɪ
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Near-close_near-back_rounded_vowel" title="Near-close near-back rounded vowel">
          ʊ
         </a>
        </span>
        ]
       </span>
       , which are heard by outsiders as variants of
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /i, u/
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Both of those features are viewed as strongly non-standard by other speakers.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Allophones">
        Allophones
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Allophones">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Phonetic nasalization occurs for vowels occurring between nasal consonants or when preceding a syllable-final nasal, e.g.
       <i>
        cinco
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈθĩŋko]
       </span>
       ('five').
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carrera256_49-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-carrera256-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Arguably, Eastern Andalusian and Murcian Spanish have ten phonemic vowels, with each of the above vowels paired by a lowered or fronted and lengthened version, e.g.
       <i>
        la madre
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [la ˈmaðɾe]
       </span>
       ('the mother') vs.
       <i>
        las madres
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [læ̞ː ˈmæ̞ːðɾɛː]
       </span>
       ('the mothers').
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, these are more commonly analyzed as allophones triggered by an underlying
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       that is subsequently deleted.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Exact_number_of_allophones">
        Exact number of allophones
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Exact number of allophones">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       There is no agreement among scholars on how many vowel allophones Spanish has; an often
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       postulated number is five
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Close_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close front unrounded vowel">
          i
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Close_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close back rounded vowel">
          u
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Mid front unrounded vowel">
          e̞
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Mid back rounded vowel">
          o̞
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Open_central_unrounded_vowel" title="Open central unrounded vowel">
          a̠
         </a>
        </span>
        ]
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Some scholars,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       however, state that Spanish has
       <i>
        eleven
       </i>
       allophones: the close and mid vowels have close
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Close_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close front unrounded vowel">
          i
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Close_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close back rounded vowel">
          u
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close-mid front unrounded vowel">
          e
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close-mid back rounded vowel">
          o
         </a>
        </span>
        ]
       </span>
       and open
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Near-close_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Near-close front unrounded vowel">
          i̞
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Near-close_back_rounded_vowel" title="Near-close back rounded vowel">
          u̞
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Open-mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open-mid front unrounded vowel">
          ɛ
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Open-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Open-mid back rounded vowel">
          ɔ
         </a>
        </span>
        ]
       </span>
       allophones, whereas
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /a/
       </span>
       appears in palatal
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open front unrounded vowel">
         a
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       , central
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Open_central_unrounded_vowel" title="Open central unrounded vowel">
         a̠
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       and velar
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Open_back_unrounded_vowel" title="Open back unrounded vowel">
         ɑ
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       variants. These symbols appear only in the narrowest variant of phonetic transcription; in more broad variants, only the symbols
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [i, u, e, o, a]
       </span>
       are used,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and that is the convention adopted in this article as well (save for this section, for the sake of clarity).
      </p>
      <p>
       Tomás Navarro Tomás describes the distribution of said eleven allophones as follows:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Close vowels
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /i, u/
        </span>
        <ul>
         <li>
          The close allophones are phonetically close
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [
           <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
            <a href="/wiki/Close_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close front unrounded vowel">
             i
            </a>
           </span>
           ,
           <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
            <a href="/wiki/Close_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close back rounded vowel">
             u
            </a>
           </span>
           ]
          </span>
          , and appear in open syllables, e.g. in the words
          <i>
           l
           <b>
            i
           </b>
           bre
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈliβɾe]
          </span>
          'free' and
          <i>
           s
           <b>
            u
           </b>
           bir
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [suˈβir]
          </span>
          'to raise'
         </li>
         <li>
          The open allophones are phonetically near-close
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [
           <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Near-close_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Near-close front unrounded vowel">
             i̞
            </a>
           </span>
           ,
           <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Near-close_back_rounded_vowel" title="Near-close back rounded vowel">
             u̞
            </a>
           </span>
           ]
          </span>
          , and appear:
          <ul>
           <li>
            In closed syllables, e.g. in the word
            <i>
             f
             <b>
              i
             </b>
             n
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [fi̞n]
            </span>
            'end'
           </li>
           <li>
            In both open and closed syllables when in contact with
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /r/
            </span>
            , e.g. in the words
            <i>
             r
             <b>
              i
             </b>
             co
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ˈri̞ko]
            </span>
            'rich' and
            <i>
             r
             <b>
              u
             </b>
             bio
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ˈru̞βjo]
            </span>
            'blond'
           </li>
           <li>
            In both open and closed syllables when before
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /x/
            </span>
            , e.g. in the words
            <i>
             h
             <b>
              i
             </b>
             jo
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ˈi̞xo]
            </span>
            'son' and
            <i>
             p
             <b>
              u
             </b>
             jó
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [pu̞ˈxo]
            </span>
            's/he bid'
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        Mid front vowel
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /e/
        </span>
        <ul>
         <li>
          The close allophone is phonetically close-mid
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [
           <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close-mid front unrounded vowel">
            e
           </a>
           ]
          </span>
          , and appears:
          <ul>
           <li>
            In open syllables, e.g. in the word
            <i>
             d
             <b>
              e
             </b>
             do
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ˈdeðo]
            </span>
            'finger'
           </li>
           <li>
            In closed syllables when before
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /m, n, t, θ, s/
            </span>
            , e.g. in the word
            <i>
             Val
             <b>
              e
             </b>
             ncia
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ba̠ˈlenθja̠]
            </span>
            'Valencia'
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
         <li>
          The open allophone is phonetically open-mid
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [
           <a href="/wiki/Open-mid_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open-mid front unrounded vowel">
            ɛ
           </a>
           ]
          </span>
          , and appears:
          <ul>
           <li>
            In open syllables when in contact with
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /r/
            </span>
            , e.g. in the words
            <i>
             gu
             <b>
              e
             </b>
             rra
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ˈɡɛra̠]
            </span>
            'war' and
            <i>
             r
             <b>
              e
             </b>
             to
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ˈrɛto]
            </span>
            <i>
             challenge
            </i>
           </li>
           <li>
            In closed syllables when not followed by
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /m, n, t, θ, s/
            </span>
            , e.g. in the word
            <i>
             b
             <b>
              e
             </b>
             lga
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ˈbɛlɣa̠]
            </span>
            'Belgian'
           </li>
           <li>
            In the diphthong
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /ei/
            </span>
            , e.g. in the words
            <i>
             p
             <b>
              ei
             </b>
             ne
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ˈpɛine]
            </span>
            'comb' and
            <i>
             r
             <b>
              ey
             </b>
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ˈrɛi]
            </span>
            <i>
             king
            </i>
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        Mid back vowel
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /o/
        </span>
        <ul>
         <li>
          The close allophone is phonetically close-mid
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [
           <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close-mid back rounded vowel">
            o
           </a>
           ]
          </span>
          , and appears in open syllables, e.g. in the word
          <i>
           c
           <b>
            o
           </b>
           m
           <b>
            o
           </b>
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈkomo]
          </span>
          'how'
         </li>
         <li>
          The open allophone is phonetically open-mid
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [
           <a href="/wiki/Open-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Open-mid back rounded vowel">
            ɔ
           </a>
           ]
          </span>
          , and appears:
          <ul>
           <li>
            In closed syllables, e.g. in the word
            <i>
             c
             <b>
              o
             </b>
             n
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [kɔn]
            </span>
            'with'
           </li>
           <li>
            In both open and closed syllables when contact with
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /r/
            </span>
            , e.g. in the words
            <i>
             c
             <b>
              o
             </b>
             rr
             <b>
              o
             </b>
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ˈkɔrɔ]
            </span>
            'I run',
            <i>
             barr
             <b>
              o
             </b>
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ˈbarɔ]
            </span>
            'mud', and
            <i>
             r
             <b>
              o
             </b>
             ble
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ˈrɔβle]
            </span>
            'oak'
           </li>
           <li>
            In both open and closed syllables when before
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /x/
            </span>
            , e.g. in the word
            <i>
             <b>
              o
             </b>
             jo
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ˈɔxo]
            </span>
            'eye'
           </li>
           <li>
            In the diphthong
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /oi/
            </span>
            , e.g. in the word
            <i>
             h
             <b>
              oy
             </b>
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ɔi]
            </span>
            'today'
           </li>
           <li>
            In stressed position when preceded by
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /a/
            </span>
            and followed by either
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /ɾ/
            </span>
            or
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /l/
            </span>
            , e.g. in the word
            <i>
             ah
             <b>
              o
             </b>
             ra
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ɑˈɔɾa̠]
            </span>
            'now'
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        Open central vowel
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /a/
        </span>
        <ul>
         <li>
          The palatal allophone is phonetically front
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [
           <a href="/wiki/Open_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Open front unrounded vowel">
            a
           </a>
           ]
          </span>
          , and appears:
          <ul>
           <li>
            Before palatal consonants, e.g. in the word
            <i>
             desp
             <b>
              a
             </b>
             cho
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [desˈpatʃo]
            </span>
            'office'
           </li>
           <li>
            In the diphthong
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /ai/
            </span>
            , e.g. in the word
            <i>
             <b>
              ai
             </b>
             re
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ˈaiɾe]
            </span>
            'air'
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
         <li>
          The velar allophone is phonetically back
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [
           <a href="/wiki/Open_back_unrounded_vowel" title="Open back unrounded vowel">
            ɑ
           </a>
           ]
          </span>
          , and appears:
          <ul>
           <li>
            Before the back vowels
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /u, o/
            </span>
            , e.g. in the word
            <i>
             fl
             <b>
              a
             </b>
             uta
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [ˈflɑuta̠]
            </span>
            'flute'
           </li>
           <li>
            In closed syllables before
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /l/
            </span>
            , e.g. in the word
            <i>
             s
             <b>
              a
             </b>
             l
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [sɑl]
            </span>
            'salt'
           </li>
           <li>
            In both open and closed syllables when before
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             /x/
            </span>
            , e.g. in the word
            <i>
             t
             <b>
              a
             </b>
             jada
            </i>
            <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
             [tɑˈxa̠ða̠]
            </span>
            'chop'
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
         <li>
          The central allophone
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [
           <a href="/wiki/Open_central_unrounded_vowel" title="Open central unrounded vowel">
            a̠
           </a>
           ]
          </span>
          appears in all other cases, e.g. in the word
          <i>
           c
           <b>
            a
           </b>
           s
           <b>
            a
           </b>
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ˈka̠sa̠]
          </span>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       According to Eugenio Martínez Celdrán, however, systematic classification of Spanish allophones is impossible due to the fact that their occurrence varies from speaker to speaker and from region to region. According to him, the exact degree of openness of Spanish vowels depends not so much on the phonetic environment, but rather on various external factors accompanying speech.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Diphthongs_and_triphthongs">
