       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">

         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center; float: right;">
       <caption>

        </b>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carrera256_49-2">

         </a>
        </sup>
       </caption>

         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ai/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         aire
        </td>
        <td>

        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /au/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         pausa
        </td>
        <td>
         pause
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ei/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         rey
        </td>
        <td>
         king
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /eu/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         neutro
        </td>
        <td>
         neutral
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /oi/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         hoy
        </td>
        <td>
         today
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ou/
         </span>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
          <a href="#cite_note-58">
           [58]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         bou
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Seine_fishing" title="Seine fishing">
          seine fishing
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="3">
         Rising
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ja/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         hacia
        </td>
        <td>
         towards
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /je/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         tierra
        </td>
        <td>
         earth
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /jo/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         radio
        </td>
        <td>
         radio
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ju/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         viuda
        </td>
        <td>
         widow
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /wa/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         cuadro
        </td>
        <td>
         picture
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /we/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         fuego
        </td>
        <td>
         fire
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /wi/
         </span>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
          <a href="#cite_note-59">
           [59]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         buitre
        </td>
        <td>
         vulture
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /wo/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         cuota
        </td>
        <td>
         quota
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Spanish has six falling
       <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">
        diphthongs
       </a>
       and eight rising diphthongs. While many diphthongs are historically the result of a recategorization of vowel sequences (hiatus) as diphthongs, there is still lexical contrast between diphthongs and
       <a href="/wiki/Hiatus_(linguistics)" title="Hiatus (linguistics)">
        hiatus
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are also some lexical items that vary amongst speakers and dialects between hiatus and diphthong: words like
       <i>
        biólogo
       </i>
       ('biologist') with a potential diphthong in the first syllable and words like
       <i>
        diálogo
       </i>
       with a stressed or pretonic sequence of
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /i/
       </span>
       and a vowel vary between a diphthong and hiatus.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="#CITEREFChițoranHualde2007">
        Chițoran &amp; Hualde (2007)
       </a>
       hypothesize that this is because vocalic sequences are longer in these positions.
      </p>
      <p>
       In addition to
       <a href="/wiki/Synalepha" title="Synalepha">
        synalepha
       </a>
       across word boundaries, sequences of vowels in hiatus become diphthongs in fast speech; when this happens, one vowel becomes non-syllabic (unless they are the same vowel, in which case they fuse together) as in
       <i>
        poeta
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈpo̯eta]
       </span>
       ('poet') and
       <i>
        maestro
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈma̯estɾo]
       </span>
       ('teacher').
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Similarly, the relatively rare diphthong
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /eu/
       </span>
       may be reduced to
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [u]
       </span>
       in certain unstressed contexts, as in
       <i>
        Eufemia
       </i>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [uˈfemja]
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the case of verbs like
       <i>
        aliviar
       </i>
       ('relieve'), diphthongs result from the suffixation of normal verbal morphology onto a stem-final
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /j/
       </span>
       (that is,
       <i>
        aliviar
       </i>
       would be |
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        alibj
       </span>
       | + |
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ar
       </span>
       |).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This contrasts with verbs like
       <i>
        ampliar
       </i>
       ('to extend') which, by their verbal morphology, seem to have stems ending in
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /i/
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Spanish also possesses
       <a href="/wiki/Triphthong" title="Triphthong">
        triphthongs
       </a>
       like
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /wei/
       </span>
       and, in dialects that use a second person plural conjugation,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /jai/
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /jei/
       </span>
       , and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /wai/
       </span>
       (e.g.
       <i>
        buey
       </i>
       , 'ox';
       <i>
        cambiáis
       </i>
       , 'you change';
       <i>
        cambiéis
       </i>
       , '(that) you may change'; and
       <i>
        averiguáis
       </i>
       , 'you ascertain').
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Non-syllabic
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /e/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /o/
       </span>
       can be reduced to
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ʝ]
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [w̝]
       </span>
       , as in
       <i>
        beatitud
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [bʝatiˈtuð]
       </span>
       ('beatitude') and
       <i>
        poetisa
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [pw̝eˈtisa]
       </span>
       ('poetess'), respectively; similarly, non-syllabic
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /a/
       </span>
       can be completely elided, as in (e.g.
       <i>
        ahorita
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [oˈɾita]
       </span>
       'right away'). The frequency (though not the presence) of this phenomenon differs amongst dialects, with a number having it occur rarely and others exhibiting it always.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Prosody">
        Prosody
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Prosody">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Spanish is usually considered a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syllable-timed_language#Syllable_timing" title="Syllable-timed language">
        syllable-timed language
       </a>
       . Even so, stressed syllables can be up to 50% longer in duration than non-stressed syllables.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Although pitch, duration, and loudness contribute to the perception of stress,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       pitch is the most important in isolation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Primary stress occurs on the
       <a href="/wiki/Ultima_(linguistics)" title="Ultima (linguistics)">
        penultima
       </a>
       (the next-to-last syllable) 80% of the time. The other 20% of the time, stress falls on the ultima and antepenultima (third-to-last syllable).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lleó_73-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lleó-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Nonverbs are generally
       <a href="/wiki/Stress_(linguistics)" title="Stress (linguistics)">
        stressed
       </a>
       on the penultimate syllable for vowel-final words and on the final syllable of consonant-final words. Exceptions are marked orthographically (see below), whereas regular words are underlyingly phonologically marked with a stress feature [+stress].
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In addition to exceptions to these tendencies, particularly learned words from Greek and Latin that feature antepenultimate stress, there are numerous
       <a href="/wiki/Minimal_pair" title="Minimal pair">
        minimal pairs
       </a>
       which contrast solely on stress such as
       <i>
        sábana
       </i>
       ('sheet') and
       <i>
        sabana
       </i>
       ('savannah'), as well as
       <i>
        límite
       </i>
       ('boundary'),
       <i>
        limite
       </i>
       ('[that] he/she limit') and
       <i>
        limité
       </i>
       ('I limited').
      </p>
      <p>
       Lexical stress may be marked orthographically with an
       <a href="/wiki/Acute_accent" title="Acute accent">
        acute accent
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        ácido
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        distinción
       </i>
       , etc.). This is done according to the mandatory stress rules of
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_orthography" title="Spanish orthography">
        Spanish orthography
       </a>
       , which are similar to the tendencies above (differing with words like
       <i>
        distinción
       </i>
       ) and are defined so as to unequivocally indicate where the stress lies in a given written word. An acute accent may also be used to differentiate homophones, such as
       <i>
        mi
       </i>
       (my), and
       <i>
        mí
       </i>
       (me). In such cases, the accent is used on the homophone that normally receives greater stress when used in a sentence.
      </p>
      <p>
       Lexical stress patterns are different between words carrying verbal and nominal inflection: in addition to the occurrence of verbal affixes with stress (something absent in nominal inflection), underlying stress also differs in that it falls on the last syllable of the inflectional stem in verbal words while those of nominal words may have ultimate or penultimate stress.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In addition, amongst sequences of clitics suffixed to a verb, the rightmost clitic may receive secondary stress, e.g.
       <i>
        búscalo
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ˈbuskaˌlo/
       </span>
       ('look for it').
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Alternations">
        Alternations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Alternations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       A number of alternations exist in Spanish that reflect diachronic changes in the language and arguably reflect
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morphophonological" title="Morphophonological">
        morphophonological
       </a>
       processes rather than strictly phonological ones. For instance, a number of words alternate between
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /k/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /θ/
       </span>
       or
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ɡ/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /x/
       </span>
       , with the latter in each pair appearing before a front vowel:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2">
         word
        </th>

        </th>
        <th colspan="2">

        </th>
        <th>
         gloss
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>

         <b>

        </td>

        </td>
       </tr>

        </td>

        </td>
       </tr>

        </td>

         </span>

         <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">
          Belgium
         </a>
         '
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         análo
         <b>

         </b>

        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /aˈnaloɡo/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'analogous'
        </td>
        <td>
         analo
         <b>
          g
         </b>
         ía
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /analoˈxia/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'analogy'
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Note that the conjugation of most verbs with a stem ending in
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /k/
       </span>
       or
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ɡ/
       </span>
       does
       <i>
        not
       </i>
       show this alternation; these segments do not turn into
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /θ/
       </span>
       or
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /x/
       </span>
       before a front vowel:
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2">
         word

        </td>

        </td>
       </tr>

          /kasˈtiɡo/

        </td>

         </span>
        </td>
