         '(that) I/he/she punish (subjunctive)'
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       There are also alternations between unstressed
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /e/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /o/
       </span>
       and stressed
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /je/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /we/
       </span>
       respectively:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2">
         word
        </th>
        <th>
         gloss
        </th>
        <th colspan="2">
         word
        </th>
        <th>
         gloss
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         h
         <b>
          e
         </b>
         ló
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /eˈlo/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'it froze'
        </td>
        <td>
         h
         <b>
          ie
         </b>
         la
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ˈʝela/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'it freezes'
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         t
         <b>
          o
         </b>
         stó
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /tosˈto/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'he toasted'
        </td>
        <td>
         t
         <b>
          ue
         </b>
         sto
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ˈtwesto/
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'I toast'
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Likewise, in a very small number of words, alternations occur between the palatal sonorants
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʎ ɲ/
       </span>
       and their corresponding alveolar sonorants
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /l n/
       </span>
       (
       <i>
        doncella
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        doncel
       </i>
       'maiden'/'youth',
       <i>
        desdeñar
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        desdén
       </i>
       'to scorn'/'scorn'). This alternation does not appear in verbal or nominal inflection (that is, the plural of
       <i>
        doncel
       </i>
       is
       <i>
        donceles
       </i>
       , not *
       <i>
        doncelles
       </i>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This is the result of geminated
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ll/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /nn/
       </span>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        Vulgar Latin
       </a>
       (the origin of
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʎ/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ɲ/
       </span>
       , respectively) degeminating and then depalatalizing in coda position.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pensado_80-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Pensado-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Words without any palatal-alveolar allomorphy are the result of historical borrowings.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pensado_80-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Pensado-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Other alternations include
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ks/
       </span>
       ~
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /x/
       </span>
       (
       <i>
        ane
        <b>
         x
        </b>
        o
       </i>
       vs
       <i>
        ane
        <b>
         j
        </b>
        o
       </i>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /kt/
       </span>
       ~
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /tʃ/
       </span>
       (
       <i>
        no
        <b>
         ct
        </b>
        urno
       </i>
       vs
       <i>
        no
        <b>
         ch
        </b>
        e
       </i>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Here the forms with
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ks/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /kt/
       </span>
       are historical borrowings and the forms with
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /x/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /tʃ/
       </span>
       forms are inherited from Vulgar Latin.
      </p>
      <p>
       There are also pairs that show antepenultimate stress in nouns and adjectives but penultimate stress in synonymous verbs (
       <i>
        vómito
       </i>
       'vomit' vs.
       <i>
        vomito
       </i>
       'I vomit').
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Phonotactics">
        Phonotactics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Phonotactics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           needs additional citations for
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            verification
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit">
            improve this article
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (April 2016)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Spanish syllable structure can be summarized as follows; parentheses enclose optional components:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        (C
        <sub>
         1
        </sub>
        (C
        <sub>
         2
        </sub>
        )) (S
        <sub>
         1
        </sub>
        ) V (S
        <sub>
         2
        </sub>
        ) (C
        <sub>
         3
        </sub>
        (C
        <sub>
         4
        </sub>
        ))
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Spanish
       <a href="/wiki/Syllable#Structure" title="Syllable">
        syllable structure
       </a>
       consists of an optional syllable onset, consisting of one or two consonants; an obligatory syllable nucleus, consisting of a vowel optionally preceded by and/or followed by a
       <a href="/wiki/Semivowel" title="Semivowel">
        semivowel
       </a>
       ; and an optional syllable coda, consisting of one or two consonants. The following restrictions apply:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Onset
        <ul>
         <li>
          First consonant (C
          <sub>
           1
          </sub>
          ): Can be any consonant, including a liquid (
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /l, r/
          </span>
          ).
         </li>
         <li>
          Second consonant (C
          <sub>
           2
          </sub>
          ): If and only if the first consonant is a stop
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /p, t, k, b, d, ɡ/
          </span>
          or a voiceless labiodental fricative
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /f/
          </span>
          , a second consonant, always a liquid
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /l, r/
          </span>
          , is permitted. Onsets
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /tl/
          </span>
          and
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /dl/
          </span>
          occur only in loanwords.
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        Nucleus
        <ul>
         <li>
          Semivowel (S
          <sub>
           1
          </sub>
          )
         </li>
         <li>
          Vowel (V)
         </li>
         <li>
          Semivowel (S
          <sub>
           2
          </sub>
          )
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        Coda
        <ul>
         <li>
          First consonant (C
          <sub>
           3
          </sub>
          ): Can be any consonant
         </li>
         <li>
          Second consonant (C
          <sub>
           4
          </sub>
          ): Must be
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /s/
          </span>
          . A coda combination of two consonants appears only in loanwords (mainly from Classical Latin) but never in words inherited from Vulgar Latin.
         </li>
         <li>
          Medial codas assimilate place features of the following onsets and are often stressed.
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lleó278_84-0">
           <a href="#cite_note-Lleó278-84">
            [84]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Maximal onsets include
       <i>
        <b>
         tr
        </b>
        ansporte
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /tɾansˈpor.te/
       </span>
       ,
       <i>
        <b>
         fl
        </b>
        aco
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ˈfla.ko/
       </span>
       ,
       <i>
        <b>
         cl
        </b>
        ave
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ˈkla.be/
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Maximal nuclei include
       <i>
        b
        <b>
         uey
        </b>
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /buei/
       </span>
       ,
       <i>
        Urug
        <b>
         uay
        </b>
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /u.ɾuˈɡuai/
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Maximal codas include
       <i>
        i
        <b>
         ns
        </b>
        talar
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ins.taˈlar/
       </span>
       ,
       <i>
        pe
        <b>
         rs
        </b>
        pectiva
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /pers.pekˈti.ba/
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In many dialects, a coda cannot be more than one consonant (one of n, r, l or s) in informal speech. Realizations like
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /trasˈpor.te/
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /is.taˈlar/
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /pes.pekˈti.ba/
       </span>
       are very common, and in many cases, they are allowed even in formal speech.
      </p>
      <p>
       Because of the phonotactic constraints, an epenthetic
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /e/
       </span>
       is inserted before word-initial clusters beginning with
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       (e.g.
       <i>
        escribir
       </i>
       'to write') but not word-internally (
       <i>
        transcribir
       </i>
       'to transcribe'),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       thereby moving the initial
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       to a separate syllable. The epenthetic
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /e/
       </span>
       is pronounced even when it is not reflected in spelling (e.g. the surname of
       <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Slim" title="Carlos Slim">
        Carlos Slim
       </a>
       is pronounced
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /esˈlin/
       </span>
       ). While Spanish words undergo word-initial epenthesis, cognates in Latin and Italian do not:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Lat.
        <i>
         status
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ˈsta.tus/
        </span>
        ('state') ~ It.
        <i>
         stato
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ˈsta.to/
        </span>
        ~ Sp.
        <i>
         <b>
          e
         </b>
         stado
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /esˈta.do/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Lat.
        <i>
         splendidus
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ˈsplen.di.dus/
        </span>
        ('splendid') ~ It.
        <i>
         splendido
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ˈsplen.di.do/
        </span>
        ~ Sp.
        <i>
         <b>
          e
         </b>
         spléndido
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /esˈplen.di.do/
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        Fr.
        <i>
         slave
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /slav/
        </span>
        ('Slav') ~ It.
        <i>
         slavo
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ˈsla.vo/
        </span>
        ~ Sp.
        <i>
         <b>
          e
         </b>
         slavo
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /esˈla.bo/
        </span>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Spanish syllable structure is phrasal, resulting in syllables consisting of phonemes from neighboring words in combination, sometimes even resulting in elision. The phenomenon is known in Spanish as
       <i>
        enlace
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For a brief discussion contrasting Spanish and English syllable structure, see
       <a href="#CITEREFWhitley2002">
        Whitley (2002
       </a>
       :32–35).
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisition_as_a_first_language">
        Acquisition as a first language
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Acquisition as a first language">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">
        Phonology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Phonology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Phonological_development" title="Phonological development">
        Phonological development
       </a>
       varies greatly by individual, both those developing regularly and those with delays. However, a general pattern of acquisition of phonemes can be inferred by the level of complexity of their features, i.e. by sound classes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A hierarchy may be constructed, and if a child is capable of producing a discrimination on one level, he/she will also be capable of making the discriminations of all prior levels.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The first level consists of stops (without a voicing distinction), nasals,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [l]
        </span>
        , and optionally, a non-lateral approximant. This includes a
        <a href="/wiki/Labial_consonant" title="Labial consonant">
         labial
        </a>
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Coronal_consonant" title="Coronal consonant">
         coronal
        </a>
        place difference (for example,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [b]
        </span>
        vs
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [t]
        </span>
        and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [l]
        </span>
        vs
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [β]
        </span>
        ).
       </li>
       <li>
        The second level includes voicing distinction for oral stops and a
        <a href="/wiki/Coronal_consonant" title="Coronal consonant">
         coronal
        </a>
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Dorsal_consonant" title="Dorsal consonant">
         dorsal
        </a>
        place difference. This allows for distinction between
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [p]
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [t]
        </span>
        , and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [k]
        </span>
        , along with their voiced counterparts, as well as distinction between
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [l]
        </span>
        and the approximant
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [j]
        </span>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        The third level includes fricatives and/or affricates.
       </li>
       <li>
        The fourth level introduces liquids other than
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [l]
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ɹ]
        </span>
        and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ɾ]
        </span>
        . It also introduces
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [θ]
        </span>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        The fifth level introduces the trill
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [r]
        </span>
        .
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       This hierarchy is based on production only, and is a representation of a child’s capacity to produce a sound, whether that sound is the correct target in adult speech or not. Thus, it may contain some sounds that are not included in the adult phonology, but produced as a result of error.
      </p>
      <p>
       Spanish-speaking children will accurately produce most
       <a href="/wiki/Segment_(linguistics)" title="Segment (linguistics)">
        segments
       </a>
       at a relatively early age. By around three-and-a-half years, they will no longer productively use phonological processes the majority of the time. Some common error patterns (found 10% or more of the time) are
       <a href="/wiki/Cluster_reduction" title="Cluster reduction">
        cluster reduction
       </a>
       , liquid simplification, and stopping. Less common patterns (evidenced less than 10% of the time) include
       <a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(sound_change)" title="Palatalization (sound change)">
        palatal fronting
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assimilation_(linguistics)" title="Assimilation (linguistics)">
        assimilation
       </a>
       , and final
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deletion_(phonology)" title="Deletion (phonology)">
        consonant deletion
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Typical phonological analyses of Spanish consider the consonants
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /b/
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /d/
       </span>
       , and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ɡ/
       </span>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/Underlying_representation" title="Underlying representation">
        underlying phonemes
       </a>
       and their corresponding approximants
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [β]
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ð]
       </span>
       , and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ɣ]
       </span>
       allophonic and derivable by
       <a href="/wiki/Phonological_rule" title="Phonological rule">
        phonological rules
       </a>
       . However, approximants may be the more basic form because monolingual Spanish-learning children learn to produce the continuant contrast between
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [p t k]
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [β ð ɣ]
       </span>
       before they do the lead voicing contrast between
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [p t k]
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [b d ɡ]
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Macken80b_90-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Macken80b-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (In comparison, English-learning children are able to produce adult-like voicing contrasts for these stops well before age three.)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The allophonic distribution of
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [b d ɡ]
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [β ð ɣ]
       </span>
       produced in adult speech is not learned until after age two and not fully mastered even at age four.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Macken80b_90-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Macken80b-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_trill" title="Alveolar trill">
        alveolar trill
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [r]
       </span>
       is one of the most difficult sounds to be produced in Spanish and as a result is acquired later in development.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Research suggests that the alveolar trill is acquired and developed between the ages of three and six years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some children acquire an adult-like trill within this period and some fail to properly acquire the trill. The attempted trill sound of the poor trillers is often perceived as a series of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_flap" title="Alveolar flap">
        taps
       </a>
       owing to hyperactive tongue movement during production.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The trill is also very difficult for those learning Spanish as a second language, sometimes taking over a year to produce properly.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Codas">
        Codas
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Codas">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       One research study found that children acquire medial
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syllable_coda" title="Syllable coda">
        codas
       </a>
       before final codas, and stressed codas before unstressed codas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since medial codas are often stressed and must undergo place assimilation, greater importance is accorded to their acquisition.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lleó278_84-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lleó278-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liquid_(linguistics)" title="Liquid (linguistics)">
        Liquid
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nasal_stop" title="Nasal stop">
        nasal
       </a>
       codas occur word medially and at the ends of frequently-used function words, so they are often acquired first.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Prosody_2">
        Prosody
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Prosody">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Research suggests that children overgeneralize stress rules when they are reproducing novel Spanish words and that they have a tendency to stress the penultimate syllables of antepenultimately stressed words, to avoid a violation of nonverb stress rules that they have acquired.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many of the most frequent words heard by children have irregular stress patterns or are verbs, which violate nonverb stress rules.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This complicates stress rules until ages three to four, when stress acquisition is essentially complete, and children begin to apply these rules to novel irregular situations.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dialectal_variation">
        Dialectal variation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Dialectal variation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Some features, such as the pronunciation of voiceless stops
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /p t k/
       </span>
       , have no dialectal variation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cotton55_100-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cotton55-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, there are numerous other features of pronunciation that differ from dialect to dialect.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Ye.C3.ADsmo">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Yeísmo">
        <i>
         Yeísmo
        </i>
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Yeísmo">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Ye%C3%ADsmo" title="Yeísmo">
        Yeísmo
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       One notable dialectal feature is the merging of the
       <a href="/wiki/Voiced_palatal_fricative" title="Voiced palatal fricative">
        voiced palatal fricative
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Voiced_palatal_fricative#Palatal" title="Voiced palatal fricative">
         ʝ
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       (as in
       <i>
        a
        <b>
         y
        </b>
        er
       </i>
       ) with the
       <a href="/wiki/Palatal_lateral_approximant" title="Palatal lateral approximant">
        palatal lateral approximant
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Palatal_lateral_approximant" title="Palatal lateral approximant">
         ʎ
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       (as in
       <i>
        ca
        <b>
         ll
        </b>
        e
       </i>
       ) into one phoneme (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Ye%C3%ADsmo" title="Yeísmo">
         yeísmo
        </a>
       </i>
       ), with
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʎ/
       </span>
       losing its laterality. While the distinction between these two sounds has traditionally been a feature of Castilian Spanish, this merger has spread throughout most of Spain in recent generations, particularly outside of regions in close linguistic contact with Catalan and Basque.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In Spanish America, most dialects are characterized by this merger, with the distinction persisting mostly in parts of Peru, Bolivia, Paraguay, and northwestern Argentina.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the other parts of Argentina, the phoneme resulting from the merger is realized as
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Voiced_postalveolar_fricative" title="Voiced postalveolar fricative">
         ʒ
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carrera258_8-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-carrera258-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and in
       <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">
        Buenos Aires
       </a>
       the sound has recently been devoiced to
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_postalveolar_fricative" title="Voiceless postalveolar fricative">
         ʃ
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       among the younger population; the change is spreading throughout Argentina.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Seseo.2C_ceceo_and_distinci.C3.B3n">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Seseo,_ceceo_and_distinción">
        <i>
         Seseo
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         ceceo
        </i>
        and
        <i>
         distinción
        </i>
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Seseo, ceceo and distinción">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seseo" title="Seseo">
        Seseo
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IberianSeseo2a.PNG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="661" data-file-width="1058" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/IberianSeseo2a.PNG/300px-IberianSeseo2a.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/IberianSeseo2a.PNG/450px-IberianSeseo2a.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/IberianSeseo2a.PNG/600px-IberianSeseo2a.PNG 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IberianSeseo2a.PNG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map showing the presence or absence of
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [θ]
         </span>
         in the
         <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">
          Iberian Peninsula
         </a>
         . Areas in light green are either
         <i>
          seseo
         </i>
         zones for Spanish and Galician or areas where other languages, not having the
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [s] / [θ]
         </span>
         contrast, are spoken
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Speakers in northern and central Spain, including the variety prevalent on radio and television, have both
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /θ/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       (
       <i>
        distinción
       </i>
       , 'distinction'). However, speakers in Latin America, Canary Islands and some parts of southern Spain have only
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       (
       <i>
        seseo
       </i>
       ), which in southernmost Spain is pronounced
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [θ]
       </span>
       and not
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [s]
       </span>
       (
       <i>
        ceceo
       </i>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carrera258_8-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-carrera258-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span id="Realization_of_.2Fs.2F">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Realization_of_/s/">
        Realization of
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /s/
        </span>
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Realization of /s/">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The phoneme
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       has three different pronunciations depending on the dialect area:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carrera258_8-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-carrera258-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dalbor_1980_37-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Dalbor_1980-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        An
        <a href="/wiki/Apical_consonant" title="Apical consonant">
         apical
        </a>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_retracted_sibilant" title="Voiceless alveolar retracted sibilant">
         alveolar retracted fricative
        </a>
        (or "
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apico-alveolar_consonant" title="Apico-alveolar consonant">
         apico-alveolar
        </a>
        " fricative)
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [s̺]
        </span>
        sounds a bit like English
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ʃ/
        </span>
        and is characteristic of the northern and central parts of
        <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
         Spain
        </a>
        and is also used by many speakers in Colombia's
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antioquia_department" title="Antioquia department">
         Antioquia department
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
         <a href="#cite_note-105">
          [105]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
         <a href="#cite_note-106">
          [106]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        A
        <a href="/wiki/Laminal_consonant" title="Laminal consonant">
         laminal
        </a>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_grooved_fricative" title="Voiceless alveolar grooved fricative">
         alveolar grooved fricative
        </a>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [s]
        </span>
        , much like the most common pronunciation of English
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /s/
        </span>
        , is characteristic of western Andalusia (e.g.
        <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga" title="Málaga">
         Málaga
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">
         Seville
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">
         Cádiz
        </a>
        ), Canary Islands, and Latin America.
       </li>
       <li>
        An
        <a href="/wiki/Apical_consonant" title="Apical consonant">
         apical
        </a>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_corono-dentoalveolar_sibilant" title="Voiceless corono-dentoalveolar sibilant">
         dental grooved fricative
        </a>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [s̄]
        </span>
        (ad hoc symbol), which has a lisping quality and sounds something like a cross between English
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /s/
        </span>
        and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /θ/
        </span>
        but is different from the
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /θ/
        </span>
        occurring in dialects that distinguish
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /s/
        </span>
        and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /θ/
        </span>
        . It occurs in eastern Andalusia like in
        <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">
         Granada
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Huelva" title="Huelva">
         Huelva
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Spain" title="Córdoba, Spain">
         Córdoba
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Ja%C3%A9n,_Spain" title="Jaén, Spain">
         Jaén
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Almer%C3%ADa" title="Almería">
         Almería
        </a>
        . It occurs only in dialects with
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ceceo" title="Ceceo">
         ceceo
        </a>
        .
       </li>
      </ol>
      <p>
       Obaid describes the apico-alveolar sound as follows:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
        <a href="#cite_note-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        There is a Castilian
        <i>
         s
        </i>
        , which is a voiceless, concave, apicoalveolar fricative: the tip of the tongue turned upward forms a narrow opening against the alveoli of the upper incisors. It resembles a faint
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ʃ/
        </span>
        and is found throughout much of the northern half of Spain.
       </p>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       Dalbor describes the apico-dental sound as follows:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
        <a href="#cite_note-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <blockquote class="templatequote">
       <p>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [s̄]
        </span>
        is a voiceless, corono-dentoalveolar groove fricative, the so-called
        <i>
         s coronal
        </i>
        or
        <i>
         s plana
        </i>
        because of the relatively flat shape of the tongue body.... To this writer, the coronal
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [s̄]
        </span>
        , heard throughout Andalusia, should be characterized by such terms as "soft," "fuzzy," or "imprecise," which, as we shall see, brings it quite close to one variety of
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /θ/
        </span>
        .... Canfield has referred, quite correctly, in our opinion, to this
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [s̄]
        </span>
        as "the lisping coronal-dental," and Amado Alonso remarks how close it is to the post-dental
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [θ̦]
        </span>
        , suggesting a combined symbol
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [θ
         <sup>
          ṣ
         </sup>
         ]
        </span>
        to represent it.
       </p>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       In some dialects,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       may become the approximant
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ɹ]
       </span>
       in the syllable coda (e.g.
       <i>
        doscientos
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [doɹˈθjẽn̪tos]
       </span>
       'two hundred').
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
        <a href="#cite_note-109">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In many places, it
       <a href="/wiki/Debuccalization" title="Debuccalization">
        debuccalizes
       </a>
       to
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [h]
       </span>
       in final position (e.g.
       <i>
        niños
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈnĩɲoh]
       </span>
       'children'), or before another consonant (e.g.
       <i>
        fósforo
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈfohfoɾo]
       </span>
       'match') so the change occurs in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syllable_coda" title="Syllable coda">
        coda
       </a>
       position in a syllable.
      </p>
      <p>
       From an autosegmental point of view, the
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       phoneme in Madrid is defined only by its
       <i>
        voiceless
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        fricative
       </i>
       features. Thus, the point of articulation is not defined and is determined from the sounds following it in the word or sentence. In Madrid, the following realizations are found:
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /pesˈkado/
       </span>
       &gt;
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [pexˈkao]
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ˈfosfoɾo/
       </span>
       &gt;
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈfofːoɾo]
       </span>
       . In parts of southern Spain, the only feature defined for
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       appears to be
       <i>
        voiceless
       </i>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
        <a href="#cite_note-110">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       it may lose its oral articulation entirely to become
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [h]
       </span>
       or even a geminate with the following consonant (
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈmihmo]
       </span>
       or
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈmĩmːo]
       </span>
       from
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ˈmismo/
       </span>
       'same').
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
        <a href="#cite_note-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In Eastern Andalusian and Murcian Spanish, word-final
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /s/
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /θ/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /x/
       </span>
       (phonetically
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [h]
       </span>
       ) regularly weaken, and the preceding vowel is lowered and lengthened:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vicente_112-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Vicente-112">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /is/
        </span>
        &gt;
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [i̞ː]
        </span>
        e.g.
        <i>
         mis
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [mi̞ː]
        </span>
        ('my' pl)
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /es/
        </span>
        &gt;
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ɛː]
        </span>
        e.g.
        <i>
         mes
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [mɛː]
        </span>
        ('month')
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /as/
        </span>
        &gt;
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [æ̞ː]
        </span>
        e.g.
        <i>
         más
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [mæ̞ː]
        </span>
        ('plus')
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /os/
        </span>
        &gt;
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ɔː]
        </span>
        e.g.
        <i>
         tos
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [tɔː]
        </span>
        ('cough')
       </dd>
       <dd>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /us/
        </span>
        &gt;
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [u̞ː]
        </span>
        e.g.
        <i>
         tus
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [tu̞ː]
        </span>
        ('your' pl)
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       A subsequent process of
       <a href="/wiki/Vowel_harmony" title="Vowel harmony">
        vowel harmony
       </a>
       takes place so
       <i>
        lejos
       </i>
       ('far') is
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈlɛxɔ]
       </span>
       ,
       <i>
        tenéis
       </i>
       ('you [plural] have') is
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [tɛˈnɛi]
       </span>
       and
       <i>
        tréboles
       </i>
       ('clovers') is
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈtɾɛβɔlɛ]
       </span>
       or
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈtɾɛβolɛ]
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
        <a href="#cite_note-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Coda_simplification">
        Coda simplification
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Coda simplification">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Southern European Spanish (Andalusian Spanish, Murcian Spanish, etc.) and several lowland dialects in Latin America (such as those from the Caribbean, Panama, and the Atlantic coast of Colombia) exhibit more extreme forms of simplification of coda consonants:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        word-final dropping of
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /s/
        </span>
        (e.g.
        <i>
         compás
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [kõmˈpa]
        </span>
        'musical beat' or 'compass')
       </li>
       <li>
        word-final dropping of nasals with nasalization of the preceding vowel (e.g.
        <i>
         ven
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [bẽ]
        </span>
        'come')
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /r/
        </span>
        in the infinitival morpheme (e.g.
        <i>
         comer
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [koˈme]
        </span>
        'to eat')
       </li>
       <li>
        the occasional dropping of coda consonants word-internally (e.g.
        <i>
         doctor
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [doˈto(r)]
        </span>
        'doctor').
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guitart_114-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Guitart-114">
          [114]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       The dropped consonants appear when additional suffixation occurs (e.g.
       <i>
        compa
        <b>
         s
        </b>
        es
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [kõmˈpase]
       </span>
       'beats',
       <i>
        ve
        <b>
         n
        </b>
        ían
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [beˈni.ã]
       </span>
       'they were coming',
       <i>
        come
        <b>
         r
        </b>
        emos
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [komeˈɾemo]
       </span>
       'we will eat'). Similarly, a number of coda assimilations occur:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /l/
        </span>
        and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /r/
        </span>
        may neutralize to
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [j]
        </span>
        (e.g.
        <a href="/wiki/Cibao" title="Cibao">
         Cibaeño
        </a>
        Dominican
        <i>
         celda
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         cerda
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ˈsejða]
        </span>
        'cell'/'bristle'), to
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [l]
        </span>
        (e.g. Caribbean Spanish
        <i>
         alma
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         arma
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ˈalma]
        </span>
        'soul'/'weapon', Andalusian Spanish
        <i>
         sartén
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [salˈtẽ]
        </span>
        ), to
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [r]
        </span>
        (e.g. Andalusian Spanish
        <i>
         alma
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         arma
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ˈarma]
        </span>
        ) or, by complete regressive assimilation, to a copy of the following consonant (e.g.
        <i>
         pulga
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         purga
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ˈpuɡːa]
        </span>
        'flea'/'purge',
        <i>
         carne
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ˈkãnːe]
        </span>
        'meat').
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guitart_114-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-Guitart-114">
          [114]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /s/
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /x/
        </span>
        , (and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /θ/
        </span>
        in southern Peninsular Spanish) and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /f/
        </span>
        may be debuccalized or elided in the coda (e.g.
        <i>
         los amigos
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [lo(h) aˈmiɣo(h)]
        </span>
        'the friends').
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guitart1_115-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Guitart1-115">
          [115]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Stops and nasals may be realized as velar (e.g. Cuban and Venezuelan
        <i>
         étnico
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ˈeɡniko]
        </span>
        'ethnic',
        <i>
         himno
        </i>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ˈĩŋno]
        </span>
        ).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guitart1_115-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-Guitart1-115">
          [115]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Final
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /d/
       </span>
       dropping (e.g.
       <i>
        mitad
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [miˈta]
       </span>
       'half') is general in most dialects of Spanish, even in formal speech.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The deletions and neutralizations show variability in their occurrence, even with the same speaker in the same utterance, so nondeleted forms exist in the underlying structure.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
        <a href="#cite_note-116">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The dialects may not be on the path to eliminating coda consonants since deletion processes have been existing for more than four centuries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
        <a href="#cite_note-117">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="#CITEREFGuitart1997">
        Guitart (1997)
       </a>
       argues that it is the result of speakers acquiring multiple phonological systems with uneven control like that of second language learners.
      </p>
      <p>
       In Standard European Spanish, the voiced obstruents
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /b, d, ɡ/
       </span>
       before a pause are devoiced and laxed to
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_bilabial_approximant" title="Voiceless bilabial approximant">
          β̥˕
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_dental_approximant" title="Voiceless dental approximant">
          ð̥˕
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_approximant" title="Voiceless velar approximant">
          ɣ̊˕
         </a>
        </span>
        ]
       </span>
       , as in
       <i>
        clu
        <b>
         b
        </b>
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [kluβ̥˕]
       </span>
       ('[social] club'),
       <i>
        se
        <b>
         d
        </b>
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [seð̥]
       </span>
       ('thirst'),
       <i>
        zigza
        <b>
         g
        </b>
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [θiɣˈθaɣ̊˕]
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
        <a href="#cite_note-118">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, word-final
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /b/
       </span>
       is rare, and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ɡ/
       </span>
       even more so. They are restricted mostly to loanwords and foreign names, such as the first name of former
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Madrid" title="Real Madrid">
        Real Madrid
       </a>
       sports director
       <a href="/wiki/Predrag_Mijatovi%C4%87" title="Predrag Mijatović">
        Predrag Mijatović
       </a>
       , which is pronounced
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ˈpɾeð̞ɾaɣ̊˕]
       </span>
       ; and after another consonant, the voiced obstruent may even be deleted, as in
       <i>
        iceberg
       </i>
       , pronounced
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [iθeˈβeɾ]
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
        <a href="#cite_note-119">
         [119]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Loan_sounds">
        Loan sounds
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Loan sounds">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The fricative
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ʃ/
       </span>
       may also appear in borrowings from other languages, such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nahuatl_language" title="Nahuatl language">
        Nahuatl
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blanch29_120-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-blanch29-120">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
        <a href="#cite_note-121">
         [121]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In addition, the affricates
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_sibilant_affricate" title="Voiceless alveolar sibilant affricate">
         ts
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_lateral_affricate" title="Voiceless alveolar lateral affricate">
         tɬ
        </a>
        /
       </span>
       also occur in Nahuatl borrowings.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blanch29_120-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-blanch29-120">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>

       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_phonology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Notes">

        </a>

        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">
       <ol class="references">

         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

         </span>

           </i>

          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Random+House+Unabridged+Dictionary&amp;rft.pub=Random+House+Inc.&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpanish+phonology">

        <li id="cite_note-2">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

         </span>

            The American Heritage Dictionary of the English Language
           </i>
           (4th ed.), Houghton Mifflin Company, 2006
          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+American+Heritage+Dictionary+of+the+English+Language&amp;rft.edition=4th&amp;rft.pub=Houghton+Mifflin+Company&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpanish+phonology">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-3">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-3">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation">
           <i>
            Webster's Revised Unabridged Dictionary
           </i>
           , MICRA, Inc., 1998
          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Webster%27s+Revised+Unabridged+Dictionary&amp;rft.pub=MICRA%2C+Inc.&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpanish+phonology">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-4">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-4">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation encyclopaedia">
           <a class="external text" href="http://encarta.msn.com/dictionary_1861595345/Castilian.html" rel="nofollow">
            <i>
             Encarta World English Dictionary
            </i>
           </a>
           . Bloomsbury Publishing Plc. 2007
           <span class="reference-accessdate">
            . Retrieved
            <span class="nowrap">
             2008-08-05
            </span>
           </span>
           .
          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Encarta+World+English+Dictionary&amp;rft.pub=Bloomsbury+Publishing+Plc.&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fencarta.msn.com%2Fdictionary_1861595345%2FCastilian.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpanish+phonology">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-5">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-5">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#CITEREFMartínez_CeldránFernández_PlanasCarrera_Sabaté2003">
           Martínez Celdrán, Fernández Planas &amp; Carrera Sabaté (2003
          </a>
          :255)
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-6">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-6">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          The continuant allophones of Spanish
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /b, d, ɡ/
          </span>
          have been traditionally described as voiced
          <i>
           fricatives
          </i>
          (e.g.
          <a href="#CITEREFNavarro_Tomás1918/1982">
           Navarro Tomás &amp; 1918/1982
          </a>
          , who (in §100) describes the air friction of
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ð]
          </span>
          as being "
          <i>
           tenue y suave
          </i>
          " ('weak and smooth');
          <a href="#CITEREFHarris1969">
           Harris (1969)
          </a>
          ;
          <a href="#CITEREFDalbor1969/1997">
           Dalbor &amp; 1969/1997
          </a>
          ; and
          <a href="#CITEREFMacpherson1975">
           Macpherson (1975
          </a>
          :62), who describes
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [β]
          </span>
          as being "...with audible friction"). However, they are more often described as
          <i>
           approximants
          </i>
          in recent literature, such as
          <a href="#CITEREFD'IntronoDel_TesoWeston1995">
           D'Introno, Del Teso &amp; Weston (1995)
          </a>
          ;
          <a href="#CITEREFMartínez_CeldránFernández_PlanasCarrera_Sabaté2003">
           Martínez Celdrán, Fernández Planas &amp; Carrera Sabaté (2003)
          </a>
          ; and
          <a href="#CITEREFHualde2005">
           Hualde (2005
          </a>
          :43). The difference hinges primarily on air turbulence caused by extreme narrowing of the opening between
          <a href="/wiki/Manner_of_articulation" title="Manner of articulation">
           articulators
          </a>
          , which is present in fricatives and absent in approximants.
          <a href="#CITEREFMartínez_Celdrán2004">
           Martínez Celdrán (2004)
          </a>
          displays a sound spectrogram of the Spanish word
          <i>
           abogado
          </i>
          showing an absence of turbulence for all three consonants.
         </span>
        </li>

           </b>

          </i>

           </b>

          </i>

          </span>

          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">

          </span>

          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">

          </span>

          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
