        <li id="cite_note-50">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-50">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#CITEREFHarris1969">
           Harris (1969
          </a>
          :78, 145). Examples include words of Greek origin like
          <i>
           énfasis
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ˈenfasis/
          </span>
          ('emphasis'); the clitics
          <i>
           su
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /su/
          </span>
          ,
          <i>
           tu
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /tu/
          </span>
          ,
          <i>
           mi
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /mi/
          </span>
          ; the three Latin words
          <i>
           espíritu
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /esˈpiɾitu/
          </span>
          ('spirit'),
          <i>
           tribu
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ˈtɾibu/
          </span>
          ('tribe'), and
          <i>
           ímpetu
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ˈimpetu/
          </span>
          ('impetus'); and affective words like
          <i>
           mami
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ˈmami/
          </span>
          and
          <i>
           papi
          </i>
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ˈpapi/
          </span>
          .
         </span>
        </li>

        <li id="cite_note-58">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-58">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           /ou/
          </span>
          occurs rarely in words; another example is the proper name
          <i>
           Bousoño
          </i>
          (
          <a href="#CITEREFSaporta1956">
           Saporta 1956
          </a>
          , p. 290). It is, however, common across word boundaries as with
          <i>
           teng
           <b>
            o u
           </b>
           na casa
          </i>
          ('I have a house').
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-59">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-59">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#CITEREFHarris1969">
           Harris (1969
          </a>
          :89) points to
          <i>
           muy
          </i>
          ('very') as the one example with
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ui̯]
          </span>
          rather than
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [wi]
          </span>
          . There are also a handful of proper nouns with
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           [ui̯]
          </span>
          , exclusive to
          <i>
           Chuy
          </i>
          (a nickname) and
          <i>
           Ruy
          </i>
          . There are no minimal pairs.
         </span>
        </li>

         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Journal+of+Linguistics&amp;rft.atitle=Diachrony+and+synchrony+in+Spanish+stress&amp;rft.volume=26&amp;rft.pages=133-164&amp;rft.date=1990&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1017%2Fs0022226700014456&amp;rft.aulast=Roca&amp;rft.aufirst=Iggy&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpanish+phonology">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li>
         <cite class="citation" id="CITEREFRoca1990b">
          Roca, Iggy (1990b), "Morphology and verbal stress in Spanish",
          <i>
           Probus
          </i>

           10.1515/prbs.1990.2.3.321
          </a>
         </cite>
         <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Probus&amp;rft.atitle=Morphology+and+verbal+stress+in+Spanish&amp;rft.volume=2&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.pages=321-50&amp;rft.date=1990&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1515%2Fprbs.1990.2.3.321&amp;rft.aulast=Roca&amp;rft.aufirst=Iggy&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpanish+phonology">
          <span style="display:none;">
          </span>
